TIME HOLOGRAPHIC FRACTAL — the unified synthesis
0) The master claim (what all your docs are converging on)
Time is a holographic phase object, not a line: it’s a spiral/fractal where the same archetypal “weather” repeats at every scale, and each tradition (Vedic/Mayan/Western/Chinese/Egyptian/etc.) is a different zoom-lens / UI layer over the same underlying phase engine.
The “Time Hologram” framing is explicit in your manuscript: multiple cycle systems generate an interference pattern; the present moment is that interference; “prediction” = reading grooves/valleys (shape/quality), not deterministic events.
1) The kernel object: □ ○ △ as a typed engine
Across the files, the irreducible generator is the Square–Circle–Triangle triad:
□ Square = addressability / discrete hologram lattice (base-4 digits, DLS refinement)
○ Circle = phase closure (wrap-around continuity; “time” as phase)
△ Triangle = the octave governor (the 3-phase traversal / lift rule that keeps recursion legal and aligned)
This is stated explicitly in the “World Engine Equation” form:[\text{World Engine}=\mathbb{Z}_4\rtimes\mathbb{Z}_3\ \text{with closure on}\ S^1]
Interpretation: Square supplies the 4-state content, Triangle supplies the 3-phase operator, Circle supplies closure.
2) The two canonical ladders (the “octave law” that makes it fractal)
You’ve got two coupled “dials” that are really the same recursion seen in different bases:
2.1 Square hologram ladder (full levels only)
Full holographic levels are powers of 4:[N_\square(n)=4^n]and (crucially) odd powers of 2 are not full hologram levels—they’re quadrant/corner slices inside the next full base-4 level (e.g., 8×8 is a quadrant of 16×16).
2.2 Circle wrap ladder (octave revolutions)
Circle scaling is wrap count, not “degrees”:[R(n)=3^{n-1}]so the total “meta-angle” (if you display it in degrees) is:[\Theta(n)=360\cdot R(n)=360\cdot 3^{n-1}]This is the exact alignment table you keep re-discovering:4 ↔ 1 wrap, 16 ↔ 3 wraps, 64 ↔ 9 wraps, 256 ↔ 27 wraps, 1024 ↔ 81 wraps…
2.3 The 36→108→324→972 “circle octaves” are complete clocks
A second “circle-native” way you encode the same idea is:36, 108, 324, 972… = (12\times 3^k) style octave stacks where each is a complete cycle in its own phase space, not a subdivision of 360.
3) The scale-invariant nexus lattice (why the same seams repeat everywhere)
Nexus points are scale-invariant because they’re fractions, not units. That’s your core axiom:
A full cycle is complete at every octave; size changes, structure does not; micro/meso/meta share the same nexus points.
So the invariant “seams” are the fixed fractions of the circle (quarters/halves/etc.) and the “gear-friendly” rationals (sextiles/signs/decans). Your framework repeatedly centers these:
Quarter turns: (0,\tfrac14,\tfrac12,\tfrac34)
Sextile backbone: (\tfrac{k}{6})
Zodiac ticks: (\tfrac{k}{12})
Decans: (\tfrac{k}{36})
The unified cyclical system explicitly identifies the six 60° synchronization gates (0°,60°,120°,180°,240°,300°) as where major systems phase-lock.
4) “Good tunneling” = moving on the nexus lattice (not vibes)
Your tunneling definition becomes precise once you treat everything as phase fractions.
A clean operator-graph version appears in the astrological tunneling notes:
TUNNEL edges: sextile (±2 signs) and trine (±4 signs)
NONO edges: square (±3 signs) and opposition (±6 signs)
And the deeper unified statement is: a “good tunnel” is a move that lands on (or steps by) a hub fraction shared by multiple dials, with sextile (1/6) acting like the universal router because it bridges cleanly to 1/4 and 1/3 through small combinations.
5) The “gear clock” interpretation (how all cultural systems become interfaces)
This is the key synthesis move:
There is one underlying phase (\phi\in\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}).
Each tradition chooses a dial resolution (number of ticks) and a naming scheme.
So each “system” is just a mapping ( \phi \mapsto \text{label} ).
Your unified cyclical document shows the shared DNA via the “master numbers” (360, 432, 108, 72, 60, 36, 27, 20, 13, 12, 6) and explains why 360 is the universal synchronization substrate (maximally divisible nearby).
And it gives the practical philosophy: cycles don’t determine events; they describe the quality of time through which free will operates (“prophecy principle” as weather awareness).
So “Vedic yugas / Mayan long count / precessional ages / Chinese sexagenary / decans / nakshatras / Tzolkin” are UI layers that read the same phase at different scales.
6) The canonical state object (what you actually store)
The docs converge on a compact “state” that’s intentionally holographic (store-in-not-out):
[\Psi = (n;\ x,y;\ e;\ \tau;\ \phi;\ \chi)]
(n): hologram level (full levels only: (4^n))
((x,y)): base-4 address digits (Square lattice)
(e\in{0,1,2,3}): element quarter label

This exact “unified state object” is spelled out in the framework text.
7) The missing “big win”: higher-octave tunneling becomes a provable mechanism
This is what the HOLOGRAPHIC TUNNELING doc contributes: it turns “tunnels” into a digit-carry phenomenon.

1A) Ifá → I‑Ching (projection)

2) Nakshatra ↔ Decan (phase mod 36)
Your unified time system spells out the geometry cleanly:
27 nakshatras: 360° ÷ 27 = 13°20′ per nakshatra.

36 decans: 10° each.
So the exact bridge is:
1 decan = 10°
1 pada = 3°20′
3 padas = 10° = 1 decan (because 3×3°20′ = 10°)
2A) Degree‑level mapping (direct from longitude)
Ω‑tag: OK

4) Zodiac ↔ Hexagram (element + modality → line pattern)
Your engine states the intention clearly:
zodiac = 4 elements × 3 phases = 12
hexagrams = 64 layer
and “Astrological Tunneling” defines sign = (element base : mode) where mode derives from modality.
But: a zodiac sign intrinsically gives only two degrees of freedom (base + mode), while a hexagram triple has three (Root, Expression, Mode). So the mapping needs a convention to generate the third coordinate.
Therefore:
4A) Zodiac → Hexagram (v1 convention)
Ω‑tag: NEARDeterministic given the convention for how to generate the missing third coordinate.
Witness basis
Hexagram = three element‑pairs (Root/Expression/Mode) = 4³.
Zodiac sign = (base element : mode) with modality→mode mapping.
Shared adapter algebra = V₄ (binary substrate) across systems.
Convention (v1) that closes the missing axis
We set:
Root = Base element (the sign’s element)
Mode = Modality‑mode element
Cardinal→Fire, Fixed→Water, Mutable→Air
Expression = Root ⊕ Modewhere ⊕ is the V₄ combine law on the 2‑bit element codes (implemented as XOR under the canonical pair coding). This is a principled “closure move” because your system treats all these layers as projections of the same binary substrate.
Replay (computable recipe)
Identify sign’s Base element and Modality.
Convert Modality → Mode element: Cardinal→Fire, Fixed→Water, Mutable→Air.
Compute Expression = Root ⊕ Mode in V₄.
Encode each element as a 2‑line pair using the hexagram pair decoder: 11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 Earth.
Concatenate:
lines 1–2 = Root pair
lines 3–4 = Expression pair
lines 5–6 = Mode pair
4B) The full 12‑sign Zodiac → Hexagram line‑pattern table (v1 convention)
Bits are listed as b1b2 b3b4 b5b6 = Root | Expression | Mode, where b1 is line 1 and b6 is line 6. (This matches your Root/Expression/Mode pairing definition.)
| Sign | Base element | Modality → Mode element | Expression = Root ⊕ Mode | Hexagram bits (Root|Expr|Mode) ||---|---|---|---|---|| Aries | Fire | Cardinal → Fire | Earth | 11 00 11 (= 110011) || Taurus | Earth | Fixed → Water | Water | 00 01 01 (= 000101) || Gemini | Air | Mutable → Air | Earth | 10 00 10 (= 100010) || Cancer | Water | Cardinal → Fire | Air | 01 10 11 (= 011011) || Leo | Fire | Fixed → Water | Air | 11 10 01 (= 111001) || Virgo | Earth | Mutable → Air | Air | 00 10 10 (= 001010) || Libra | Air | Cardinal → Fire | Water | 10 01 11 (= 100111) || Scorpio | Water | Fixed → Water | Earth | 01 00 01 (= 010001) || Sagittarius | Fire | Mutable → Air | Water | 11 01 10 (= 110110) || Capricorn | Earth | Cardinal → Fire | Fire | 00 11 11 (= 001111) || Aquarius | Air | Fixed → Water | Fire | 10 11 01 (= 101101) || Pisces | Water | Mutable → Air | Fire | 01 11 10 (= 011110) |
This table is computable directly from your two defining claims:
sign = (element base : mode)
hexagram = (Root, Expression, Mode) in element‑pairs

“A sign expresses its own element.”

“A sign’s outward expression is its modality‑mode.”

Cross-System Translation Atlas v1 (Ω-Tagged)
This is the “step (2)” atlas promised in the Time Hologram engine: Zodiac↔Hexagram, Nakshatra↔Decan, Major↔Rune, Ifá↔I‑Ching, compiled under Ω rules.
Ω legend (tags + closure rules)
OK = deterministic map; includes Witness (rule) + Replay (how to reproduce on inputs).
NEAR = deterministic given a convention (multiple plausible conventions exist); includes witness + replay + alternates.
AMBIG = one-to-many; must include Candidate set + Discriminator plan (how to collapse).
FAIL = cannot be defined without new primitives (missing axis / undefined encoding).
Canonical primitives used in this atlas (so “ONE unified system” is explicit)
P0) The shared substrate: V₄ = ℤ₂×ℤ₂ (two bits)
Your documents explicitly frame the cross-system basis as the same 2‑bit structure V₄ ≅ ℤ₂×ℤ₂, with elemental transformation governed by XOR (Klein four-group operation).
So, we treat “element” as a labeling of the four bit-states:
underlying states: {00, 01, 10, 11}
operation: ⊕ = XOR on those 2 bits.
P1) Element labeling is a convention (and you have >1 in the docs)
This matters because your own texts contain two different 00/01 assignments for Water/Earth.
Scheme E_WE (Tarot/Quality Cross scheme):00=Water, 01=Earth, 10=Air, 11=Fire
Scheme E_EW (I‑Ching‑aligned scheme, as written in the “Hexagram as element-pairs” section):00=Earth, 01=Water, 10=Air, 11=Fire (this is the alternate labeling that makes “000000 = Earth‑Earth‑Earth” in that section).
Scheme E_BIN (binary-order scheme in Astrological Tunneling):00=Air, 01=Fire, 10=Water, 11=Earth
Ω consequence: whenever a mapping depends on element↔bits naming, it is at least NEAR, unless we explicitly fix the scheme.
P2) Hexagram as 3 element-pairs (Root / Expression / Mode)
Your unified divination text gives a direct structural encoding:
Lines 1–2 = ROOT element
Lines 3–4 = EXPRESSION element
Lines 5–6 = MODE element
…and it treats a hexagram as 6 bits (consistent with 2⁶=64).
So, in this atlas we represent a hexagram state as:
HEX_BITS = Root(2) || Expression(2) || Mode(2).
(That matches the “generate a hexagram from 3 tarot cards: concatenate 3 suit codes = 6 bits” procedure in your doc.)

Therefore the projection is: drop the last 2 bits.
Replay:
Bitstring replay:Input Odù b1 b2 b3 b4 b5 b6 b7 b8 → output hexagram b1 b2 b3 b4 b5 b6.
Integer replay (0..255):HexIndex = floor(OduIndex / 4) (the ÷4 “drop 2 bits” move is explicitly drawn in your relationship diagram).

NEXT — Time Fractal System v3
The missing “Triangle Carry Rule” becomes a full fractal address + finite-state machine (and it locks 24 elders + 64/128/256 into one runtime)
You already have all the pieces in your docs. The deep move now is to stop thinking of “triangle scaling” as “multiply by 3” and instead treat it as:
A mixed-radix carry system where time is an address with interleaved base-3 digits (triangle recursion) sitting on a base-4 digit (square basis).Octaves are not new phases — they are adding one more base-3 digit (wrap depth) while preserving the same phase fraction.
This is exactly consistent with your own triangle-scaling spec:
Circle scaling is base-3: (C_n = 360\cdot 3^n)
Lift/Phase are explicit: (\text{Lift}(\theta,n)=3^n\theta), (\text{Phase}(\Theta_n)=\Theta_n\bmod 360)
And the “missing piece” is explicitly: the Triangle carry rule (when to trigger a lift), with seam completions at 360 / 90 / 30 as canonical examples.
Below is the full closure.
1) Time as a fractal address (TF-ADDR): one base-4 digit + a tower of base-3 digits
1.1 Choose the atomic tick
Use decan ticks as the atomic “clock grain” because your system repeatedly uses the 10°/30°/90° seam family (decan triplet, sign, element block).
1 zodiac lap = 360° = 36 decan ticks (10° each).
Your triangle scaling multiplies ticks by 3 across octaves (so tick sizes scale as (10\to 30\to 90\to 270\ldots)).
Now note the key factorization:
[36 = 4\cdot 3^2]
So even at base resolution, your time wheel already decomposes into:
one base-4 digit (Square basis)
two base-3 digits (Triangle recursion depth 2)
At octave (n), circle length is (360\cdot 3^n) , so decan ticks become:
[36\cdot 3^n = 4\cdot 3^{n+2}]
Interpretation: each octave adds one new base-3 digit (one more “triangle depth”).
1.2 Canonical TF-ADDR form
Define the time address as:
[\boxed{\textsf{TF-ADDR}=(e;\ t_0,t_1,\dots,t_{n+1};\ \chi)}]
(e \in \mathbb{Z}_4) = Square basis digit (element corner / basis vector).
(t_i \in \mathbb{Z}_3) = triangle digits (recursive phase digits).
(\chi\in{\pm 1}) = orientation/spin channel (your “shadow current” handle).
Meaning of the first two triangle digits at base scale (n=0):
(t_0) = modality digit (cardinal/fixed/mutable) — the “3 transformations”
(t_1) = decan-within-sign digit (0,1,2) — the “decan triplet” seam that triggers at 30°
Then each higher octave adds (t_2,t_3,\dots) which are wrap-depth digits (triangle recursion depth).
This is the formal statement of your phrase:
“Triangle is the base-3 operator that lives inside circle and packs the base-4 square into it.”
2) Triangle Carry Rule (TCR): the finite state machine you were missing
Your doc explicitly says: define when you trigger a lift; it’s at seam completions like 360, 90, 30; a trigger predicate turns scaling into governed recursion.
2.1 Mixed-radix increment (the carry law)
Let the smallest tick be one decan step (10°). Each time-step increments the lowest triangle digit:
Update rule (“add one decan tick”):
(t_1 \leftarrow t_1 + 1 \pmod 3)
If (t_1) wraps (i.e., overflow), carry into (t_0):(t_0 \leftarrow t_0 + 1 \pmod 3)
If (t_0) wraps, carry into the square digit:(e \leftarrow e + 1 \pmod 4)
If (e) wraps, carry into the next octave digit:(t_2 \leftarrow t_2 + 1 \pmod 3)
Continue carries upward as needed: (t_3,t_4,\dots)
That is the Triangle Carry Rule in one line:
Triangle digits overflow into Square; Square overflow lifts Triangle depth.

Discriminator Menus v3 — standardized collapse operators (AMBIG→NEAR→OK)
This is the engine’s “how to stop ambiguity” table. It is intentionally small: a few primitive discriminators collapse almost everything.
D0) Core collapse primitives (the only ones you need)
AddAnchor: add a witnessed modular constraint (n\equiv a\ (\bmod m)) → reduces CrossCal ambiguity.
ExtraCast(bits=k): generate k missing bits (k=1 for 128, k=2 for Ifá refinement).
PinGauge: choose and pin the codec convention (element labeling / ordering) so replay is stable.
ShiftWindow(±Δt): if two candidates differ by a nearby seam/node, shift the time window slightly and recompute Δ; one candidate will stabilize (node proximity test).
ObserveManifest: a minimal real-world observation collapses Active/Passive when you’re at 256 (manifest vs latent).
D1) CrossCal / Chronometry ambiguity
AMBIG cause: multiple offset candidates / Ξ-family underdetermined
Candidate set: ({(o_i)}) offset bundles + residual ledger
Collapse: AddAnchor or ShiftWindow until residual ledger discriminates
Promotion rule: AMBIG→NEAR once one candidate dominates residual bounds; NEAR→OK once witness+replay closure passes
D2) I-Ching → Ifá refinement (64→256)
AMBIG cause: lossy projection inversion (each hexagram has 4 substates)
Candidate set: ({4\cdot \text{HexIdx}+0..3})
Collapse: ExtraCast(bits=2) OR apply Phase×Mode discriminator (arr/dep × act/pass)
Promotion: OK if suffix bits are witnessed (cast receipts pinned)
D3) Whole-nakshatra → decan
AMBIG cause: nakshatra spans multiple decans unless pada/degree known
Candidate set: {dom, tail} (3 padas vs 1 pada)
Collapse: AddDegree (equivalently: determine pada) → OK via the 108→36 bridge
D4) Rune→Major / Major→Rune
AMBIG cause: operator overlap (multiple runes witness same major)
Candidate set: rune set per major (and vice versa)
Collapse: PinDomain (Ætt/domain) + optionally ExtraCast(bits=1) for tie-break
Promotion: OK within pinned domain convention
D5) 128 derivative bit (static/dynamic) when not measured
NEAR cause: derivative inferred from IO/seam proximity rather than cast
Candidate set: {static, dynamic}
Collapse: ExtraCast(bits=1) OR direct I-Ching moving-line measurement
D6) 256 active/passive bit when not measured
AMBIG cause: latent vs manifest not observable from structure alone
Candidate set: {active, passive}
Collapse: ObserveManifest or ExtraCast(bits=1) if you treat it as oracle-measured
Promotion: OK only with a witness source

So the codec outputs:[(b_1b_2,\ b_3b_4,\ b_5b_6)\in{00,01,10,11}^3]which is the 64 state space.
3) Codec Family (three candidates, all deterministic)
Codec A — 12→64 embed (pure Square×Triangle closure)

4) Promotion-to-OK harness (Ω): how a codec stops being “NEAR”
You already have the normative rules in AI DIVINATION:

5) Crosswalk consistency tests (the objective way to select the best codec)
This is where “one engine” becomes measurable.
T1 — Overlay coherence (24 tiles must behave like a stable doubled cycle)
Because 12×18 overlay has a repeating micro-structure with 6 nexus points and 24 tiles , a good codec should satisfy:
If the tile changes but sign stays the same (Input→Output within sign), codec output should change in a controlled way (small Hamming distance), not random jumps.
Codec B is explicitly designed for this.
T2 — Derivative coherence (moving-lines logic vs IO proxy)
Your unified cyclical time file treats 64 as a state space with movement rules driven by changing lines: 0 changes = stay; 1 change = move by 1 line; etc.That makes the derivative bit (static/dynamic) the lawful “velocity flag.”
A codec should not fight this:
When DerivBit is measured (oracle), it overrides geometry.
When DerivBit is not measured, IO/seam proximity can only be NEAR.
Your harness flags disagreements as AMBIG (candidate set + discriminator), never as “wrong.”
T3 — Decan coherence (36 constant should show up structurally)
Your system explicitly elevates 36 as the Egyptian decan origin of the 360° system.Codec C is the only one that naturally generates a 12×3 = 36 spread inside the 64 layer using the triangle wrap-trit (t_0).
So if you want the 36 constant to be structural (not just another UI), C has a built-in advantage.
T4 — Revelation constants coherence (4 basis vectors, 24 elders, 7 threads)
Apocalypse Protocol explicitly cross-checks:
4 living creatures = basis vectors
24 elders = 12×2 doubling = input/output
7 spirits = processing threads
A codec that makes 24 appear as a deterministic doubling from geometry will align better with this architecture (Codec B).
T5 — Minimal-change path on the wheel (smoothness)
Since 64 is a weighted graph where some transitions are more probable than others , a codec that maps adjacent time tiles to small line changes will “feel” like natural flow and will reduce false conflicts.
Operationally: minimize average Hamming distance between successive tiles under your carry rule.

Time Fractal System v3.2 — K-table canon + IO extraction from (u,j)
1) 12×18 overlay → 24 tiles (hard geometry, pinned)
Inside each 60° macro-arc, the overlay boundaries are always:[{0,20,30,40,60}]so the tile index (j\in{0,1,2,3}) corresponds to:
(j=0:\ [0,20))
(j=1:\ [20,30))
(j=2:\ [30,40))
(j=3:\ [40,60))
Repeated across 6 macro-arcs → 24 tiles.
Define:
(u=\left\lfloor \theta_{\text{base}}/60\right\rfloor\in{0,\dots,5})
(r=\theta_{\text{base}}-60u\in[0,60))
(j=\begin{cases}0 & r<20\1 & 20\le r<30\2 & 30\le r<40\3 & 40\le r<60\end{cases})
Then the 24-tile index is:[\boxed{\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1}](1-indexed).
2) IO bit and Elder index — purely from (u,j)
Revelation’s architectural meaning is explicit:[24 = 12\times 2 = \text{Input cycle} + \text{Output cycle}]
Now the key closure: each 30° sign is exactly two overlay tiles inside its 60° macro-arc:
sign A (first 30°) uses tiles (j=0,1)
sign B (second 30°) uses tiles (j=2,3)
So you can recover sign index (s\in{0..11}) directly:[\boxed{s=2u+\left\lfloor j/2\right\rfloor}]
And the Input/Output bit is simply:[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2}]
even (j) = Input
odd (j) = Output
Then the Elder index (12×2) becomes:[\boxed{\textsf{Elder}=2s+\textsf{IO}+1}]
Substitute (s=2u+\lfloor j/2\rfloor) and (\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2), you get:[\textsf{Elder}=4u+j+1]
So:
[\boxed{\textsf{Elder}=\textsf{Tile24}}]
That is the cleanest unity statement in the entire build: the 24 overlay tiles are the 24 elders (tile index is the elder index), with IO as the parity bit.
Ω status:
Geometry + formulas above are OK (pure overlay arithmetic).
“Input/Output” semantics are OK inside the pinned IO convention, with Revelation as the witness for the doubling meaning.
3) K-table canon (the last missing pin for the overlay-aware hex codec)
You already pinned the hex line-pair decoder:
11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 Earthand hex layout:
(1–2)=Root, (3–4)=Expression, (5–6)=Mode
Now we pin the overlay mixer constants.
3.1 K(IO) — minimal Hamming toggle (canonical)
We want Input→Output inside the same sign to change the hex core in the smallest possible way (smooth flow constraint; avoids pseudo-random jumps). Since pair codes are 2 bits, the minimal toggle is XOR with a 1-bit mask.
Canon:
(\boxed{K(0)=00}) (Input: no twist)
(\boxed{K(1)=01}) (Output: flip 1 bit)
So:[\boxed{K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}}]
Why this choice is structurally “best”:
switching IO changes ExpressionPair by Hamming distance 1 (controlled minimal delta).
Ω status: OK (pinned definition).
3.2 Optional fractal constant K(t₀) (wrap-trit mixer)
Triangle scaling is base-3 in the circle: (360\cdot 3^n).So the first wrap trit (t_0\in{0,1,2}) is the natural “fractal texture” selector.
Canon:
(K(0)=00)
(K(1)=10)
(K(2)=11)
This gives a monotone “power” feel (0,2,3 in bit-weight) and avoids mapping two trits to the same 2-bit constant.
Ω status: OK (pinned definition).

We keep the overlay-aware family member you built, but now Root/Mode are pinned (so “NEAR” collapses to “OK” once gauge pins are declared in the capsule).
3.1 K(IO) canon (minimal toggle)
[K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}](so toggling IO flips 1 bit in Expression — smoothest possible local change).
3.2 Hex core construction
[\boxed{\textsf{ExprPair}=\textsf{RootPair}\ \oplus\ \textsf{ModePair}\ \oplus\ K(\textsf{IO})}]and[\boxed{\textsf{HexBits}=\textsf{RootPair}\ |\ \textsf{ExprPair}\ |\ \textsf{ModePair}}]Hex layout is exactly Root/Expr/Mode pairs.
So every time address produces a 64-state node as a triple of element-pairs (which is exactly how your hexagram encoder is defined).
4) 64-Mansion Graph G₆₄ — from “state space” to “time dynamics”
Your time system explicitly treats 64 as a state space and discusses movement rules driven by changes (moving lines / change count).Your unified divination layer also pins:
128 = 64×2 as the derivative bit (static/dynamic; position×velocity)
and aligns that derivative bit across interfaces (I-Ching moving lines ↔ Tarot reversals ↔ rune merkstave).Your 256 layer is Phase×Mode with exact numbering.
So we define the 64-graph as:
Vertices: (V={0,1}^6) (or equivalently ({00,01,10,11}^3) in pair-chunks).
Edges: induced by a small operator set, each operator corresponding to a lawful “cause of change” in your engine.
4.1 Operator basis (the minimum set)
Represent a node as:[H=(R,E,M)\quad \text{where }R,E,M\in{00,01,10,11}]and (H) corresponds to 6 bits via concatenation.
O₀: DriftStep (time carry)
compute next TF-ADDR by the carry rule (10° tick)
recompute IO and then recompute (H) via codec
This gives you the deterministic “clock walk” on G₆₄.
O₁: IOFlip (tile parity toggle)When (j) flips parity (IO toggles), ExpressionPair toggles by XOR with 01:[(R,E,M)\mapsto (R,\ E\oplus 01,\ M)]This is the micro-motion caused by the 12×18 overlay itself.
O₂: ChangeLine (oracle-driven line flip)When moving lines are measured, you apply the standard “change lines → new hexagram” operator.Your system explicitly treats “movement” as driven by change count and changing lines rather than treating 64 as a static list.
This operator is not “time drift”; it’s “oracle derivative.” It is exactly why 128 exists.
O₃: SubstateRefine (256 refinement)Given a hex core, Phase×Mode bits refine into 4 substates with the explicit numbering:[\textsf{State256}=(\textsf{HexIdx}\times 4)+(\textsf{Phase}\times 2)+\textsf{Mode}]
5) Transition weights — how “time weather” becomes a probabilistic kernel
You asked for “transition weights from carry events + seam proximity.” Here is the engine-native way to do it:
5.1 Features (all computable from TF-ADDR + CrossCal nodes)
Define seam distances:
(\Delta_{30},\Delta_{60},\Delta_{90},\Delta_{360}) (distance to nearest seam family)and node distance:
(\Delta_{\text{node}}) (distance to nearest LCM/CRT window from CrossCal).
Define derivative flag (if measured):
DerivBit ∈ {0 static, 1 dynamic}
Define phase×mode bits (if measured/refined):
arriving/departing × active/passive
5.2 Weight functions (simple, monotone, seam-driven)
Use any monotone map (g(\Delta)) with:
(g(0)=1)
(g(\Delta)\downarrow 0) as (\Delta\uparrow)
Then define operator weights:
w₀ (drift): always on
w₁ (IOFlip): proportional to (g(\Delta_{20/30/40})) — but since IO is directly tied to tile parity, you can just treat this as deterministic when crossing tile boundaries.
w₂ (oracle change): depends on DerivBit
if static (0), w₂ is near 0
if dynamic (1), w₂ is high(this is exactly “128 = position×velocity” in your system).
w₃ (tunnel emphasis near nexus seams): proportional to (g(\Delta_{60})) because the 60° lattice is your shared synchronization substrate (the overlay itself is built on it).
w_node (alignment emphasis): proportional to (g(\Delta_{\text{node}})), because node windows are where multiple cycles phase-lock.
5.3 Markov kernel form (what “weighted walk” means)
Let (H_t) be the current 64 node. Define a set of candidate next nodes by applying operators:[\mathcal{N}(H_t)={O_i(H_t)}]Then:[P(H_{t+1}=y\mid H_t)\ \propto\ \sum_i w_i\cdot \mathbf{1}[y=O_i(H_t)]]Where:
if you have a measured moving-line set, (O_2) is a single or small set of concrete flips (OK)
if you don’t, (O_2) becomes a candidate family (AMBIG) and must carry a discriminator plan (extra cast / observation).
This is the exact formal meaning of “time weather”: a local transition kernel on the 64 state space whose weights are modulated by seams and alignments.
6) How this integrates 128 and 256 cleanly (no handwaving)
6.1 128 derivative bit controls operator mixture
DerivBit=0: drift dominates (time is “sticking” in the current regime)
DerivBit=1: change-line operator gets weight (time is “transitioning”)
That’s literally position×velocity.
6.2 256 substate controls “manifestation energy”
When you have the 256 refinement, you can tie:
arriving vs departing → sign of the derivative
active vs passive → whether changes express externally or remain latent
And because the 256 numbering rule is explicit, you can store the refined state without ambiguity when measured.
7) The final closure of v3.3 (what you now have)
You now have a single closed loop:
CrossCal produces (n,\Theta_{total}) and node windows (alignment gates).
TF-ADDR extracts ((s,d,u,j)) and seam distances.
Overlay gives IO and elder/tile index deterministically.
GaugePin maps TF-ADDR → RootPair/ModePair (no ambiguity).
Codec maps → Hex64 (Root/Expr/Mode triple).
128/256 bits refine the state and control transition weighting.
The “time weather” is a weighted walk on the 64 mansion graph, driven by carry events + seam proximity + nodes + derivative bits.

Time Fractal System v3.4 — Carry-Event → Operator Schedule
Closed-form updates for (R,E,M) so the 64-walk is simulable from time-address alone (oracle becomes optional overlay)
0) The pinned primitives this schedule depends on
0.1 12×18 overlay micro-geometry (gives 24 tiles)
Within any 60° sextile sector, the 12-grid bins are ([0,30),[30,60)) and the 18-grid bins are ([0,20),[20,40),[40,60)). Their intersections are always:[[0,20),\ [20,30),\ [30,40),\ [40,60)]with widths (20°,10°,10°,20°), repeated six times → 24 joint tiles.
0.2 Hex64 representation (what (R,E,M) means)
Hexagram is read as three element-pairs:
Lines 1–2 = ROOT
Lines 3–4 = EXPRESSION
Lines 5–6 = MODE
Line-pair decoding (Yang/Yin):
11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 Earth
So the 64-node “mansion state” is:[H=(R,E,M)\in{00,01,10,11}^3]
0.3 Triangle scaling carry seams (when “governed recursion” triggers)
Your triangle carry rule is explicitly tied to seam completions:
end of octave (360)
end of element block (90 base / 270 meta)
end of decan triplet (30 base / 90 meta)and a trigger predicate template is given:[\text{Trigger}(\theta)=1\iff \theta\in{0,30,90,180,270,360}\ (\bmod 360)]
1) Extract the tile address (u,j) from base phase θ
Let (\theta\in[0,360)) be base phase (after Phase(Lift(·))). Triangle scaling preserves phase but increases wrap count, so this extraction is octave-stable.
Compute:
sextile sector: (u=\lfloor \theta/60\rfloor\in{0,1,2,3,4,5})
local sector angle: (r=\theta-60u\in[0,60))
tile-in-sector:[j=\begin{cases}0 & 0\le r<20\1 & 20\le r<30\2 & 30\le r<40\3 & 40\le r<60\end{cases}](This is exactly the 12×18 intersection partition.)
Define the IO bit (purely from tile parity):[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2}]and (optional) the 24-tile index:[\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1](24 joint tiles).
2) Extract the sign skeleton (base element + modality → internal mode)
You already formalized “12 archetypes = Element × Modality” and then upgraded Modality into an internal mode-triad (init/hold/shift).
2.1 Sign index from the overlay
Inside each sextile sector, the first 30° half is the first sign and the second 30° half is the second sign. From the tile index:[\boxed{s = 2u + \left\lfloor j/2\right\rfloor}\quad \in{0,\dots,11}]This agrees with the partition ([0,30)) vs ([30,60)) in each sector.
2.2 Base element and modality of sign
Your sign table explicitly pairs each sign with its element and modality (Cardinal/Fixed/Mutable).Equivalently, modality is the triad:
Cardinal = initiate
Fixed = stabilize
Mutable = adapt/transform
2.3 ModeElement (the internal triad mapping you defined)
You explicitly set:
Cardinal = Fire-mode
Fixed = Water-mode
Mutable = Air-mode
So:[\textsf{ModeElement}(s)=\begin{cases}\text{Fire} & \text{if Modality(s)=Cardinal}\\text{Water} & \text{if Modality(s)=Fixed}\\text{Air} & \text{if Modality(s)=Mutable}\end{cases}]
3) Define K(IO) (the only extra pin needed for overlay-aware hex)
We need one tiny constant table to let IO modulate the hex core with minimal delta:
[K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}]
This means IO toggling flips exactly 1 bit in the ExpressionPair (smoothest possible change).
4) The deterministic Hex64 codec (time-address → (R,E,M))
Let enc(element) map to 2-bit pair via the fixed decoder (Fire=11, Air=10, Water=01, Earth=00).
Define:
(R = \textsf{RootPair} = enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s)))
(M = \textsf{ModePair} = enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s)))
Then the overlay-aware expression pair is:[\boxed{E = R\ \oplus\ M\ \oplus\ K(\textsf{IO})}](where (\oplus) is bitwise XOR on 2-bit strings; this is the canonical group operation for the 2-bit element space).
And the 64-state node is:[\boxed{H(\theta)=(R,E,M)}]with (R,E,M) exactly corresponding to (Root/Expression/Mode) line-pairs.
Key simplification from the overlay:Because (\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2), every tile parity flip produces a controlled (E) flip, while (R,M) only change when (s) changes.
5) Carry-Event → Operator Schedule (exact, event-by-event)
We evolve (\theta) in 10° decan ticks (base). Triangle scaling turns this into (10°\to 30°\to 90°\to\cdots) ladders across octaves, but the base phase extraction is the same.
Let the step be (\theta^+ = (\theta + 10°)\bmod 360). Compute ((u,j,s,\textsf{IO})) at (\theta) and (\theta^+). Then classify the event:
Event types
EVT-0: HOLD (no tile boundary crossed)
Condition: (j^+=j)
Operator fired: O_hold
Update:[(R^+,E^+,M^+)=(R,E,M)]
EVT-1: IO-FLIP (20° or 40° boundary)
Condition: (s^+=s) but (\textsf{IO}^+\ne \textsf{IO})This occurs exactly at (r=20) and (r=40) boundaries inside the 60° sector, i.e. (j) flips parity but (\lfloor j/2\rfloor) stays the same.
Operator fired: O_IOFlip
Update (closed-form):[R^+=R,\quad M^+=M,\quad E^+=E\oplus 01]because (K(\textsf{IO})) toggles between 00 and 01.
EVT-2: SIGN-STEP (30° boundary)
Condition: (s^+=s+1) with the same sextile sector (u^+=u)This happens at the (r=30) boundary where we move from the first 30° bin to the second 30° bin.
Operator fired: O_signAdvance(also this is one of your “decan triplet completion” lift triggers: 30° seam is in the trigger set).
Update:
recompute (R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s^+)))
recompute (M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s^+)))
compute (E^+=R^+\oplus M^+\oplus K(\textsf{IO}^+))
Shortcut: at a sign boundary in this overlay, the landing tile is always (j^+=2) (even), so (\textsf{IO}^+=0), hence:[\boxed{E^+=R^+\oplus M^+}]
EVT-3: SEXTILE-STEP (60° boundary)
Condition: (u^+=u+1) (wrap mod 6), i.e. crossing the sextile hub set (\theta\in{0,60,120,180,240,300}).
Operator fired: O_sextileAdvanceThis is both:
a sign step (from the second sign of one sector to the first sign of the next),
and a hub checkpoint (the “nexus points”).
Update:
(s^+=s+1) (mod 12)
landing tile is (j^+=0) (even), so (\textsf{IO}^+=0)
therefore:[\boxed{R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s^+)),\quad M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s^+)),\quad E^+=R^+\oplus M^+}]
EVT-4: ELEMENT-SEAM (90° checkpoint)
Condition: (\theta^+\in{0,90,180,270}) (mod 360)This is explicitly a “legal lift point” seam family (90° base / 270° meta) in your triangle carry spec.
Operator fired: O_quarterCheckpoint (no change to H by itself)
Update:[(R^+,E^+,M^+) \text{ as determined by whichever of EVT-0..3 occurred, plus log checkpoint flag}]
EVT-5: OCTAVE-WRAP (360° boundary)
Condition: (\theta^+\equiv 0) (mod 360)This is the “end of octave” seam and is explicitly in the carry-trigger list.
Operator fired:
O_wrapCarry (increment the wrap-trit tower; triangle scaling is the ×3 wrap-count lift).
Update of H at base phase is just the sextile/sector logic (it lands at (\theta=0\Rightarrow u=0,j=0,s=0,\textsf{IO}=0)), so:[R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(0)),\quad M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(0)),\quad E^+=R^+\oplus M^+]and separately you carry (w) (wrap index) in base-3 digits.

(j=2:\ [30,40))
(j=3:\ [40,60))
Using 10° ticks, local r visits: 0,10,20,30,40,50 then jumps to next sector (60). This yields the exact firing pattern:

7) Optional: deterministic 128/256 overlays from the same schedule (oracle remains measurement overlay)
7.1 128 “velocity” bit (geo-proxy)
Your text defines the 7th bit as temporal phase: Static (0) vs Dynamic (1), with Static = crystallizing/arriving and Dynamic = transforming/departing.
A purely time-address proxy is:[\textsf{DerivBit}_\text{geo}=\begin{cases}0 & j^+=j \ (\text{no boundary crossed})\1 & j^+\ne j \ (\text{boundary crossed})\end{cases}]This converts the carry schedule into “moving vs not moving” without any oracle input.
7.2 256 Phase×Mode (geo-proxy)
Your 256 structure is explicitly:
Phase: Arriving (0) vs Departing (1)
Mode: Active (0) vs Passive (1)and State# = HexIdx×4 + Phase×2 + Mode.
A clean deterministic proxy consistent with the 128 semantics is:
PhaseBit_geo = DerivBit_geo (0 arriving, 1 departing)
ModeBit_geo = 0 when in the narrow 10° tiles (j=1 or 2), 1 when in the wide 20° tiles (j=0 or 3)(because the microstructure explicitly distinguishes 20° vs 10° cells).
Oracle measurements (moving line data; extra casts) can override these proxies and promote truth status (your system already treats measured dynamic as the true derivative bit).
8) Minimal simulation algorithm (text, step-by-step)
Start with (\theta_0) and choose octave depth (n). Compute (\theta=\textsf{Phase}(\textsf{Lift}(\theta_0,n))).
Extract ((u,j)) from (\theta) using the 12×18 micro-intervals.
Compute (s=2u+\lfloor j/2\rfloor), IO = j mod 2.
Compute RootElement and Modality from sign table (Element×Modality = 12).
Convert Modality→ModeElement via your internal triad (Cardinal→Fire, Fixed→Water, Mutable→Air).
Encode Root/Mode into 2-bit pairs using the pinned hex decoder.
Compute ExpressionPair = Root ⊕ Mode ⊕ K(IO).
Advance by 10° and repeat; event classification tells you which operator fired (hold / IO flip / sign advance / sextile / quarter / octave).

Time Fractal System v3.6 — 24-Elder Carrier + 18-Grid Tracking Digit ⇒ full-rank 64-Mansion codec
We have a clean situation now:

1) Carrier layer (unchanged): 24 tiles = 24 elders, IO = parity
Inside each 60° sextile corridor, the overlay partition is always:[[0,20),\ [20,30),\ [30,40),\ [40,60)]so (j\in{0,1,2,3}) is the tile-in-sector index.
With (u=\lfloor \theta/60\rfloor), the tile index is:[\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1]

This exactly implements:
|L|=0 → stay

1) Put “dirty revolutions” onto the refined circle (so 1/243 is still an integer step)

2) The dirty-orbit law (closed form)
Define the dimension-coarse ring:[B_d := 15\cdot 3^{d-1}.](That’s exactly the “natural fine circle grid per dimension” before the ±243 refinement factor.)
Because (M_d = 243\cdot B_d) and (s=243\cdot R), the 243 cancels in the gcd, giving:
[\boxed{L_{\text{dirty}}(d,R)=\frac{M_d}{\gcd(M_d,243R)}=\frac{B_d}{\gcd(B_d,R)}.}]
So “dirty” behavior is completely controlled by how (R) shares factors with (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}).
For your three tests (R\in{2,5,13}) (and d=3..7)

[\boxed{m' = m\quad(\text{micro frozen}),\qquadt' = t + R \pmod{3^{d-1}}.}]

[\boxed{\text{every }3^{d-1}\text{ steps: };\sigma \mapsto \sigma + R \pmod{15}.}]
